## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The equation of motion typically combines nonlinear restoring forces in x, damping terms in v, and possible periodic driving forces in t.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with drive)
- Van der Pol term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v * x**2 (mixed coupling)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (polynomial force model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — look for odd polynomial terms in x
- Even-power terms in x (x**2, x**4) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation (damping) or injection; sign of coefficient determines which
- Products of x**2 and v (e.g., x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type oscillators
- Sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- If acceleration depends only on x and v (not t), the system is autonomous and phase-plane analysis applies
- Rational functions of x like x/(1+c*x**2) can model bounded/saturating restoring forces
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x*v suggest non-conservative forces that depend on both state variables

**Candidate 39**: `c0*v*cos(c1*x + c2) + c3*cos(c4*t + c5)`

- Need `c0*v*cos(c1*x + c2) = -0.263896*v*sin(x)`. Use c1=1, c2=-π/2, c0=-0.263896 ✓ **This matches!**
